## 31. User enumeration via distinct login error responses

- Severity: low
- OWASP: A07
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/auth/login
- CVSS: 3.7 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N)

### Description
The authentication endpoint at POST /api/auth/login differentiates between non-existent accounts and valid accounts with an incorrect password by returning distinct error codes and messages. When a submitted email address does not exist in the system, the API responds with `{"code":"USER_NOT_FOUND","message":"No account found with this email address."}`. When the email exists but the supplied password is incorrect, the API responds with `{"code":"WRONG_PASSWORD","message":"Incorrect password."}`. Both responses are returned with HTTP 401. This divergence in error semantics allows an unauthenticated attacker to programmatically distinguish between registered and unregistered email addresses.

### Impact
An attacker can enumerate the full set of registered customer email addresses at scale by issuing automated requests and inspecting the response code. Valid emails can then be fed into credential-stuffing or targeted brute-force campaigns, and the resulting list of valid accounts has standalone privacy value (customer base disclosure). The finding is compounded by separately observed absence of rate-limiting and weak password hashing, but the enumeration itself is exploitable independently.

### Likelihood
High. The behavior is exposed on a public, unauthenticated endpoint, requires no special tooling, and can be scripted to iterate over large email lists quickly. No authentication, user interaction, or prior access is required.

### Recommendation
Return a single, generic response for both the invalid-email and wrong-password cases, using a uniform error code and message such as `"Invalid email or password"`. Additionally, equalize server-side response timing (e.g., perform a constant-time hash comparison even when the supplied email is absent) so that response latency cannot be used as a secondary enumeration oracle. Complement these changes with per-account and per-IP rate limiting and account lockout / CAPTCHA controls to mitigate downstream credential-stuffing risk.

### Evidence
```
Login with non-existent email returned 401 + {"code":"USER_NOT_FOUND","message":"No account found with this email address."}. Login with valid email (amelia.chen@example.com) and wrong password returned 401 + {"code":"WRONG_PASSWORD","message":"Incorrect password."}. Two distinct codes/messages allow a script to enumerate valid emails at scale.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST /api/auth/login with {"email":"nonexistent_user_xyz@example.com","password":"wrong"} vs {"email":"amelia.chen@example.com","password":"WRONG_PASSWORD"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
For invalid email: {"code":"USER_NOT_FOUND","message":"No account found with this email address."}  For wrong password: {"code":"WRONG_PASSWORD","message":"Incorrect password."}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 32. Verbose error disclosure: stack traces, absolute file paths, and source-line leakage in 500 responses

- Severity: low
- OWASP: A05
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/profile
- CVSS: 3.7 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N)

### Description
The global exception handler in public/index.php returns `$e->getMessage()`, `$e->getFile()`, `$e->getLine()`, and `$e->getTraceAsString()` to the client on every uncaught Throwable. Any code path that throws leaks absolute server paths, function names, library versions and source lines to the attacker.

### Impact
Discloses absolute server paths (e.g. /var/www/bankofed/...), internal class names (BankOfEd\Services\AuthService, BankOfEd\Middleware\AuthMiddleware, BankOfEd\Router), source filenames, and line numbers. Provides an attacker with a roadmap of the application structure, internal namespaces, and the exact entry-point chain, which materially aids exploitation of related issues (e.g. confirming AuthMiddleware logic flow when probing JWT handling).

### Likelihood
High - any unhandled exception reached by an authenticated or unauthenticated caller triggers disclosure; behavior is global to the application rather than restricted to a single endpoint.

### Recommendation
Wrap the global exception handler so production responses only emit a generic error code and a correlation ID; never include `$e->getFile()`, `$e->getLine()`, or `$e->getTraceAsString()` in the response body. Log full exception details (including file, line, and trace) server-side only, gated by an environment flag. Also disable PHP `display_errors` in production php.ini and ensure the framework is not configured with `APP_DEBUG=true` / equivalent debug mode.

### Evidence
```
Request: GET /api/profile with an Authorization header containing a JWT missing the `jti` claim. Response: 500 application/json body - {"code":"INTERNAL_ERROR","message":"BankOfEd\\Services\\AuthService::isTokenRevoked(): Argument #1 ($jti) must be of type string, null given, called in /var/www/bankofed/src/Middleware/AuthMiddleware.php on line 28","details":{"file":"/var/www/bankofed/src/Services/AuthService.php","line":77,"trace":"#0 /var/www/bankofed/src/Middleware/AuthMiddleware.php(28): BankOfEd\\Services\\AuthService::isTokenRevoked()\n#1 /var/www/bankofed/Router.php(101): ... #3 {main}"}}. Same disclosure behavior reproduced on POST /api/profile/avatar.
```

### Request Evidence
```
GET /api/profile (with Authorization header that has a malformed JWT missing `jti`)
```

### Response Evidence
```
500 application/json with file=/var/www/bankofed/src/Services/AuthService.php line=77 and full PHP call trace including internal class names.
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 33. Web server version disclosed in Server response header

- Severity: info
- OWASP: A05
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: skipped
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/health
- CVSS: 0 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:N)

### Description
Every response reveals the precise web server build: `Server: Apache/2.4.58 (Ubuntu)`. This information helps attackers correlate the server against publicly known CVEs and unsupported versions.

### Impact
Information disclosure only; helps reconnaissance but does not itself enable exploitation. Severity would rise if Apache/2.4.58 were demonstrably vulnerable to a remote, unauthenticated issue in this deployment.

### Likelihood
Always reachable; trivially harvested by any unauthenticated request.

### Recommendation
Suppress or genericize the `Server` header (e.g., `Server: WebServer` or `ServerTokens Prod` with `ServerSignature Off` in Apache) and keep Apache patched to a currently supported release.

### Evidence
```
Response header `server: Apache/2.4.58 (Ubuntu)` present on every probed request.
```

## 34. Web server version disclosed in Server response header

- Severity: info
- OWASP: A05
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: skipped
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/health
- CVSS: 0 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:N)

### Description
The Server header exposes 'Apache/2.4.58 (Ubuntu)', identifying the exact web server software and version on every response.

### Impact
Minor information disclosure that helps attackers fingerprint known CVEs; no exploitable behaviour is demonstrated from the header alone.

### Likelihood
Informational; useful as reconnaissance but not directly exploitable here.

### Recommendation
Set ServerTokens to Prod (or equivalent) and remove or override the Server header so that build/version details are not exposed.

### Evidence
